I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
`.env` file is no longer auto-imported
### Describe the bug

After updating `wxt` from `0.20.20` to `0.20.21`, this error is caused:

> Error: Missing required config: CHROME_EXTENSION_ID, FIREFOX_EXTENSION_ID

I have these environment variables defined in the `.env` file.

This is probably caused by https://github.com/wxt-dev/wxt/pull/2181

```diff
- import { config } from 'dotenv';
```

Simply importing `dotenv/config` auto-imports the `.env` file. From the [README](https://github.com/motdotla/dotenv#readme):

> ```ts
> // index.js
> require('dotenv').config()
> // or import 'dotenv/config' // for esm
> 
> console.log(`Hello ${process.env.HELLO}`)
> ```
> 
> That's it. `process.env` now has the keys and values you defined in your `.env` file.

### Reproduction

- https://github.com/hyunbinseo/better-surf/releases/tag/v0.0.28
- https://github.com/hyunbinseo/better-surf/actions/runs/24392573474/job/71242144892

_No response_

     1	import { readFileSync, existsSync } from 'node:fs';
     2	import { parseEnv } from 'node:util';
     3	import { expand } from 'dotenv-expand';
     4	import type { TargetBrowser } from '../../types';
     5	
     6	/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
     7	export function loadEnv(mode: string, browser: TargetBrowser) {
     8	  const envFiles = [
     9	    // List is ordered with general files first, specific ones last, so the more
    10	    // specific files override the more general ones in the loop below.
    11	    `.env`,
    12	    `.env.local`,
    13	    `.env.${mode}`,
    14	    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    15	    `.env.${browser}`,
    16	    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    17	    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    18	    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
    19	  ];
    20	
    21	  const parsed = Object.fromEntries<string>(
    22	    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
    23	      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
    24	
    25	      try {
    26	        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
    27	        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
    28	        return Object.entries(parsedEnv) as [string, string][];
    29	      } catch {
    30	        return [];
    31	      }
    32	    }),
    33	  );
    34	
    35	  // Make a copy of `process.env` so that `dotenv-expand` doesn't re-assign the
    36	  // expanded values to the global `process.env`.
    37	  const processEnv = { ...process.env } as Record<string, string>;
    38	
    39	  expand({
    40	    parsed,
    41	    processEnv,
    42	  });
    43	
    44	  return parsed;
    45	}
    46

    33	/**
    34	 * Given an inline config, discover the config file if necessary, merge the
    35	 * results, resolve any relative paths, and apply any defaults.
    36	 *
    37	 * Inline config always has priority over user config. Cli flags are passed as
    38	 * inline config if set. If unset, undefined is passed in, letting this function
    39	 * decide default values.
    40	 */
    41	export async function resolveConfig(
    42	  inlineConfig: InlineConfig,
    43	  command: WxtCommand,
    44	): Promise<ResolvedConfig> {

    54	    });

   250	
   251	async function resolveManifestConfig(
   252	  env: ConfigEnv,
   253	  manifest: UserManifest | Promise<UserManifest> | UserManifestFn | undefined,
   254	): Promise<UserManifest> {
   255	  return typeof manifest === 'function'
   256	    ? await manifest(env)
   257	    : await (manifest ?? {});
   258	}
   259	
   260	/**
   261	 * Merge the inline config and user config. Inline config is given priority.
   262	 * Defaults are not applied here.
   263	 */
   264	async function mergeInlineConfig(
   265	  inlineConfig: InlineConfig,
   266	  userConfig: UserConfig,
   267	): Promise<InlineConfig> {
   268	  // Merge imports option
   269	  const imports: InlineConfig['imports'] =
   270	    inlineConfig.imports === false || userConfig.imports === false
   271	      ? false
   272	      : userConfig.imports == null && inlineConfig.imports == null
   273	        ? undefined
   274	        : defu(inlineConfig.imports ?? {}, userConfig.imports ?? {});
   275	
   276	  // Merge manifest option
   277	  const manifest: UserManifestFn = async (env) => {
   278	    const user = await resolveManifestConfig(env, userConfig.manifest);
   279	    const inline = await resolveManifestConfig(env, inlineConfig.manifest);
   280	    return defu(inline, user);
   281	  };
   282	
   283	  const merged = defu(inlineConfig, userConfig);
   284	
   285	  // Builders
   286	  const builderConfig = await mergeBuilderConfig(
   287	    merged.logger ?? consola,
   288	    inlineConfig,
   289	    userConfig,
   290	  );
   291	
   292	  return {
   293	    ...merged,
   294	    // Custom merge values
   295	    imports,
   296	    manifest,
   297	    ...builderConfig,
   298	  };
   299	}
   300	
   301	function resolveZipConfig(
   302	  root: string,
   303	  browser: string,
   304	  outBaseDir: string,
   305	  mergedConfig: InlineConfig,
   306	): NullishRequired<ResolvedConfig['zip']> {
   307	  const downloadedPackagesDir = path.resolve(root, '.wxt/local_modules');
   308	  return {
   309	    name: undefined,
   310	    sourcesTemplate: '{{name}}-{{version}}-sources.zip',
   311	    artifactTemplate: '{{name}}-{{version}}-{{browser}}.zip',
   312	    sourcesRoot: root,
   313	    includeSources: [],
   314	    compressionLevel: 9,
   315	    ...mergedConfig.zip,
   316	    zipSources:
   317	      mergedConfig.zip?.zipSources ?? ['firefox', 'opera'].includes(browser),
   318	    exclude: mergedConfig.zip?.exclude ?? [],
   319	    excludeSources: [
   320	      '**/node_modules',
   321	      // WXT files
   322	      '**/web-ext.config.ts',
   323	      // Hidden files
   324	      '**/.*',
   325	      // Tests
   326	      '**/__tests__/**',
   327	      '**/*.+(test|spec).?(c|m)+(j|t)s?(x)',
   328	      // Output directory
   329	      `${path.relative(root, outBaseDir)}/**`,
   330	      // From user
   331	      ...(mergedConfig.zip?.excludeSources ?? []),
   332	    ],
   333	    downloadPackages: mergedConfig.zip?.downloadPackages ?? [],
   334	    downloadedPackagesDir,
   335	  };
   336	}
   337	
   338	function resolveAnalysisConfig(
   339	  root: string,
   340	  mergedConfig: InlineConfig,
   341	): NullishRequired<ResolvedConfig['analysis']> {
   342	  const analysisOutputFile = path.resolve(
   343	    root,
   344	    mergedConfig.analysis?.outputFile ?? 'stats.html',
   345	  );
   346	  const analysisOutputDir = path.dirname(analysisOutputFile);
   347	  const analysisOutputName = path.parse(analysisOutputFile).name;
   348	
   349	  return {
   350	    enabled: mergedConfig.analysis?.enabled ?? false,
   351	    open: mergedConfig.analysis?.open ?? false,
   352	    template: mergedConfig.analysis?.template ?? 'treemap',
   353	    outputFile: analysisOutputFile,
   354	    outputDir: analysisOutputDir,
   355	    outputName: analysisOutputName,
   356	    keepArtifacts: mergedConfig.analysis?.keepArtifacts ?? false,
   357	  };
   358	}

   506	async function getUnimportEslintOptions(
   507	  wxtDir: string,
   508	  options: InlineConfig['imports'],
   509	): Promise<ResolvedEslintrc> {
   510	  const inlineEnabled =
   511	    options === false ? false : (options?.eslintrc?.enabled ?? 'auto');
   512	
   513	  let enabled: ResolvedEslintrc['enabled'];
   514	  switch (inlineEnabled) {
   515	    case 'auto':
   516	      const version = await getEslintVersion();
   517	      let major = parseInt(version[0]);
   518	      if (isNaN(major)) enabled = false;
   519	      if (major <= 8) enabled = 8;
   520	      else if (major >= 9) enabled = 9;
   521	      // NaN
   522	      else enabled = false;
   523	      break;
   524	    case true:
   525	      enabled = 8;
   526	      break;

Now I see the issue clearly. The `loadEnv` function:

1. Reads the `.env` files and parses them
2. Uses `dotenv-expand` to expand variables
3. But it does NOT set the parsed values back into `process.env`

The comment says "Make a copy of `process.env` so that `dotenv-expand` doesn't re-assign the expanded values to the global `process.env`." - but the problem is that after expansion, the values are NOT being set on `process.env` at all.

   164	async function resolveManifestConfig(env, manifest) {
   165	        return typeof manifest === "function" ? await manifest(env) : await (manifest ?? {});
   166	}
   167	/**
   168	* Merge the inline config and user config. Inline config is given priority.
   169	* Defaults are not applied here.
   170	*/
   171	async function mergeInlineConfig(inlineConfig, userConfig) {
   172	        const imports = inlineConfig.imports === false || userConfig.imports === false ? false : userConfig.imports == null && inlineConfig.imports == null ? void 0 : defu(inlineConfig.imports ?? {}, userConfig.imports ?? {});
   173	        const manifest = async (env) => {
   174	                const user = await resolveManifestConfig(env, userConfig.manifest);
   175	                return defu(await resolveManifestConfig(env, inlineConfig.manifest), user);
   176	        };
   177	        const merged = defu(inlineConfig, userConfig);
   178	        const builderConfig = await mergeBuilderConfig(merged.logger ?? consola, inlineConfig, userConfig);
   179	        return {
   180	                ...merged,
   181	                imports,
   182	                manifest,
   183	                ...builderConfig
   184	        };
   185	}
   186	function resolveZipConfig(root, browser, outBaseDir, mergedConfig) {

   192	                sourcesRoot: root,
   193	                includeSources: [],
   194	                compressionLevel: 9,

   202	                        "**/__tests__/**",
   203	                        "**/*.+(test|spec).?(c|m)+(j|t)s?(x)",
   204	                        `${path.relative(root, outBaseDir)}/**`,
   205	                        ...mergedConfig.zip?.excludeSources ?? []
   206	                ],
   207	                downloadPackages: mergedConfig.zip?.downloadPackages ?? [],
   208	                downloadedPackagesDir
   209	        };
   210	}

   340	async function getUnimportEslintOptions(wxtDir, options) {
   341	        const inlineEnabled = options === false ? false : options?.eslintrc?.enabled ?? "auto";
   342	        let enabled;
   343	        switch (inlineEnabled) {
   344	                case "auto":
   345	                        const version = await getEslintVersion();
   346	                        let major = parseInt(version[0]);
   347	                        if (isNaN(major)) enabled = false;
   348	                        if (major <= 8) enabled = 8;
   349	                        else if (major >= 9) enabled = 9;
   350	                        else enabled = false;
   351	                        break;
   352	                case true:
   353	                        enabled = 8;
   354	                        break;
   355	                default: enabled = inlineEnabled;
   356	        }
   357	        return {
   358	                enabled,
   359	                filePath: path.resolve(wxtDir, enabled === 9 ? "eslint-auto-imports.mjs" : "eslintrc-auto-import.json"),
   360	                globalsPropValue: true
   361	        };
   362	}
   363	/** Returns the path to `node_modules/wxt`. */
   364	function resolveWxtModuleDir() {
   365	        const url = resolve("wxt", import.meta.url);
   366	        return path.resolve(fileURLToPath(url), "../..");
   367	}
   368	async function isDirMissing(dir) {

   421	                        id: absolutePath

     6	/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
     7	export function loadEnv(mode: string, browser: TargetBrowser) {
     8	  const envFiles = [
     9	    // List is ordered with general files first, specific ones last, so the more
    10	    // specific files override the more general ones in the loop below.
    11	    `.env`,
    12	    `.env.local`,
    13	    `.env.${mode}`,
    14	    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    15	    `.env.${browser}`,
    16	    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    17	    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    18	    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
    19	  ];
    20	
    21	  const parsed = Object.fromEntries<string>(
    22	    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
    23	      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
    24	
    25	      try {
    26	        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
    27	        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
    28	        return Object.entries(parsedEnv) as [string, string][];
    29	      } catch {
    30	        return [];
    31	      }
    32	    }),
    33	  );
    34	
    35	  // Make a copy of `process.env` so that `dotenv-expand` doesn't re-assign the
    36	  // expanded values to the global `process.env`.
    37	  const processEnv = { ...process.env } as Record<string, string>;
    38	
    39	  expand({
    40	    parsed,
    41	    processEnv,
    42	  });
    43	
    44	  return parsed;
    45	}

'use strict'

function _resolveEscapeSequences (value) {
  return value.replace(/\\\$/g, '$')
}

function expandValue (value, processEnv, runningParsed) {
  const env = { ...runningParsed, ...processEnv } // process.env wins

  const regex = /(?<!\\)\${([^{}]+)}|(?<!\\)\$([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)/g

  let result = value
  let match
  const seen = new Set() // self-referential checker

  while ((match = regex.exec(result)) !== null) {
    seen.add(result)

    const [template, bracedExpression, unbracedExpression] = match
    const expression = bracedExpression || unbracedExpression

    // match the operators `:+`, `+`, `:-`, and `-`
    const opRegex = /(:\+|\+|:-|-)/
    // find first match
    const opMatch = expression.match(opRegex)
    const splitter = opMatch ? opMatch[0] : null

    const r = expression.split(splitter)

    let defaultValue
    let value

    const key = r.shift()

    if ([':+', '+'].includes(splitter)) {
      defaultValue = env[key] ? r.join(splitter) : ''
      value = null
    } else {
      defaultValue = r.join(splitter)
      value = env[key]
    }

    if (value) {
      // self-referential check
      if (seen.has(value)) {
        result = result.replace(template, defaultValue)
      } else {
        result = result.replace(template, value)
      }
    } else {
      result = result.replace(template, defaultValue)
    }

    // if the result equaled what was in process.env and runningParsed then stop expanding
    if (result === runningParsed[key]) {
      break
    }

    regex.lastIndex = 0 // reset regex search position to re-evaluate after each replacement
  }

  return result
}

function expand (options) {
  // for use with progressive expansion
  const runningParsed = {}

  let processEnv = process.env
  if (options && options.processEnv != null) {
    processEnv = options.processEnv
  }

  // dotenv.config() ran before this so the assumption is process.env has already been set
  for (const key in options.parsed) {
    let value = options.parsed[key]

    // short-circuit scenario: process.env was already set prior to the file value
    if (processEnv[key] && processEnv[key] !== value) {
      value = processEnv[key]
    } else {
      value = expandValue(value, processEnv, runningParsed)
    }

    options.parsed[key] = _resolveEscapeSequences(value)

    // for use with progressive expansion
    runningParsed[key] = _resolveEscapeSequences(value)
  }

  for (const processKey in options.parsed) {
    processEnv[processKey] = options.parsed[processKey]
  }

  return options
}

module.exports.expand = expand

But actually, we WANT the expanded values to be assigned to the global `process.env`.

The original code used `import { config } from 'dotenv'` which would set values on `process.env` directly. The new code uses `dotenv-expand` which also sets values on `processEnv`. The issue is that they pass a copy of `process.env` instead of the actual `process.env`.

Actually, re-reading the PR description: the issue was that `import { config } from 'dotenv'` was replaced. The `import { config } from 'dotenv'` would auto-load the `.env` file. Now they're doing it manually but not setting the values back to `process.env`.

The fix should be to either:
1. Pass `process.env` directly to `expand` (so the expanded values get set on the real `process.env`)
2. After expansion, set the parsed values on `process.env` manually

Let me also check if there are edge cases. The comment says they made a copy to prevent dotenv-expand from re-assigning to global `process.env`. But that's exactly what we want - for the values to be available via `process.env`. However, we might want to be careful about overriding existing `process.env` values. 

Looking at the `expand` function again: 
```js
// short-circuit scenario: process.env was already set prior to the file value
if (processEnv[key] && processEnv[key] !== value) {
  value = processEnv[key]
}
```

It already respects existing `process.env` values (if they were set before, they take precedence over .env file values). So it should be safe to pass `process.env` directly.

But actually, the current behavior of passing a copy means that the expanded values are only in the copy (which is then discarded). So the `expand` function:
1. If `processEnv` is provided, uses that; otherwise uses `process.env`
2. Then at the end: `for (const processKey in options.parsed) { processEnv[processKey] = options.parsed[processKey] }`
3. It sets the expanded values onto `processEnv`

So the fix is clear: we need to pass the actual `process.env` to `expand` so the expanded values are set on the global `process.env`. Or alternatively, we can just set them manually after expansion.

2026-05-30 07:47:33,437 - INFO - swea-agent-wxt-dev__wxt-2267 - 💭 THOUGHT
Wait, I need to reconsider. Looking at the expand function more carefully:

1. The `expand` function already sets values on `processEnv` (which defaults to `process.env` if not provided)
2. But it also respects existing `process.env` values - if a key already exists in `process.env` with a different value, it keeps the existing value

So if I just call `expand({ parsed })` without providing `processEnv`, it will:
1. Use `process.env` as the processEnv
2. Set expanded values onto `process.env`
3. But NOT override existing `process.env` values (since `if (processEnv[key] && processEnv[key] !== value) { value = processEnv[key] }`)

This is actually the correct behavior! If someone has already set an environment variable externally, it should take precedence over the .env file.

But wait, there's a subtlety. The `expand` function also has this logic:
```js
// short-circuit scenario: process.env was already set prior to the file value
if (processEnv[key] && processEnv[key] !== value) {
  value = processEnv[key]
}
```

This means: if `process.env` already has a value for this key AND it differs from the parsed value, keep the process.env value. But then it still does:
```js
for (const processKey in options.parsed) {
    processEnv[processKey] = options.parsed[processKey]
}
```

Wait, this sets the expanded value (from `options.parsed[key] = _resolveEscapeSequences(value)`) onto processEnv. So if process.env already had a value, it would be overwritten by the expansion... unless the value was set to `processEnv[key]` in the short-circuit branch.

Let me trace through an example:
- `.env` file: `MY_VAR=hello`
- `process.env.MY_VAR` = `world` (already set externally)
- `parsed = { MY_VAR: "hello" }`
- In expand: `value = "hello"`, `processEnv["MY_VAR"] = "world"` (differs), so `value = "world"`
- Then `options.parsed["MY_VAR"] = "world"` (the unexpanded value gets replaced by the existing env value)
- Then `processEnv["MY_VAR"] = "world"` (no change)

So existing `process.env` values are preserved. Good.

Now if we DON'T pass `processEnv`, it defaults to `process.env`, and the values will be set on the real `process.env`. That's exactly what we want.

But actually, wait. Let me re-read the expand code more carefully:

```js
let processEnv = process.env
if (options && options.processEnv != null) {
  processEnv = options.processEnv
}
```

So if we call `expand({ parsed })` (without `processEnv`), it uses `process.env` directly, and the expanded values will be set on `process.env`. That's what we want!

But then the `for` loop I added is redundant because `expand` already does that. Let me simplify

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_env_fix.mjs << 'EOF'
import { existsSync, readFileSync, writeFileSync, unlinkSync } from 'node:fs';
import { parseEnv } from 'node:util';
import { expand } from 'dotenv-expand';

// Helper to reproduce the old behavior
function loadEnvOld(mode, browser) {
  const envFiles = [
    `.env`,
    `.env.local`,
    `.env.${mode}`,
    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    `.env.${browser}`,
    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
  ];

  const parsed = Object.fromEntries(
    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
      try {
        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
        return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
      } catch {
        return [];
      }
    }),
  );

  // OLD behavior: copy process.env so values are NOT set on real process.env
  expand({
    parsed,
    processEnv: { ...process.env }
  });

  return parsed;
}

// Helper to reproduce the NEW behavior
function loadEnvNew(mode, browser) {
  const envFiles = [
    `.env`,
    `.env.local`,
    `.env.${mode}`,
    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    `.env.${browser}`,
    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
  ];

  const parsed = Object.fromEntries(
    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
      try {
        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
        return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
      } catch {
        return [];
      }
    }),
  );

  // NEW behavior: pass process.env directly so values ARE set on real process.env
  expand({ parsed });

  return parsed;
}

// Test
const testDir = '/tmp/test-env-fix';
import { mkdirSync } from 'node:fs';
try { mkdirSync(testDir, { recursive: true }); } catch {}

const originalCwd = process.cwd();
process.chdir(testDir);

// Clean up any existing test files
try { unlinkSync('.env'); } catch {}

// Create a .env file
writeFileSync('.env', 'TEST_VAR=hello_world\nANOTHER_VAR=test123\n');

// Test OLD behavior
console.log('=== OLD behavior ===');
console.log('Before loadEnvOld:');
console.log('process.env.TEST_VAR =', process.env.TEST_VAR);
console.log('process.env.ANOTHER_VAR =', process.env.ANOTHER_VAR);

const resultOld = loadEnvOld('production', 'chrome');
console.log('Return value:', resultOld);
console.log('After loadEnvOld:');
console.log('process.env.TEST_VAR =', process.env.TEST_VAR);
console.log('process.env.ANOTHER_VAR =', process.env.ANOTHER_VAR);
console.log('OLD behavior sets env vars on process.env?', process.env.TEST_VAR === 'hello_world' ? 'YES (BUG FIXED?)' : 'NO (BUG CONFIRMED)');

// Clean up
delete process.env.TEST_VAR;
delete process.env.ANOTHER_VAR;

// Test NEW behavior
console.log('\n=== NEW behavior ===');
console.log('Before loadEnvNew:');
console.log('process.env.TEST_VAR =', process.env.TEST_VAR);
console.log('process.env.ANOTHER_VAR =', process.env.ANOTHER_VAR);

const resultNew = loadEnvNew('production', 'chrome');
console.log('Return value:', resultNew);
console.log('After loadEnvNew:');
console.log('process.env.TEST_VAR =', process.env.TEST_VAR);
console.log('process.env.ANOTHER_VAR =', process.env.ANOTHER_VAR);
console.log('NEW behavior sets env vars on process.env?', process.env.TEST_VAR === 'hello_world' ? 'YES (FIX WORKS)' : 'NO (STILL BROKEN)');

// Clean up
process.chdir(originalCwd);
EOF

import { existsSync, readFileSync } from "node:fs";
import { parseEnv } from "node:util";
import { expand } from "dotenv-expand";
//#region src/core/utils/env.ts
/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
function loadEnv(mode, browser) {
	const envFiles = [
		`.env`,
		`.env.local`,
		`.env.${mode}`,
		`.env.${mode}.local`,
		`.env.${browser}`,
		`.env.${browser}.local`,
		`.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
		`.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`
	];
	const parsed = Object.fromEntries(envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
		if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
		try {
			const parsedEnv = parseEnv(readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8"));
			return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
		} catch {
			return [];
		}
	}));
	expand({
		parsed,
		processEnv: { ...process.env }
	});
	return parsed;
}
//#endregion
export { loadEnv };

=== Source file ===
import { readFileSync, existsSync } from 'node:fs';
import { parseEnv } from 'node:util';
import { expand } from 'dotenv-expand';
import type { TargetBrowser } from '../../types';

/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
export function loadEnv(mode: string, browser: TargetBrowser) {
  const envFiles = [
    // List is ordered with general files first, specific ones last, so the more
    // specific files override the more general ones in the loop below.
    `.env`,
    `.env.local`,
    `.env.${mode}`,
    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    `.env.${browser}`,
    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
  ];

  const parsed = Object.fromEntries<string>(
    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];

      try {
        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
        return Object.entries(parsedEnv) as [string, string][];
      } catch {
        return [];
      }
    }),
  );

  // Set the parsed and expanded values on process.env, respecting any existing
  // environment variables that were already set.
  expand({ parsed });

  return parsed;
}

=== Dist file ===
import { existsSync, readFileSync } from "node:fs";
import { parseEnv } from "node:util";
import { expand } from "dotenv-expand";
//#region src/core/utils/env.ts
/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
function loadEnv(mode, browser) {
        const envFiles = [
                `.env`,
                `.env.local`,
                `.env.${mode}`,
                `.env.${mode}.local`,
                `.env.${browser}`,
                `.env.${browser}.local`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`
        ];
        const parsed = Object.fromEntries(envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
                if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
                try {
                        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8"));
                        return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
                } catch {
                        return [];
                }
        }));
        // Set the parsed and expanded values on process.env, respecting any existing
        // environment variables that were already set.
        expand({ parsed });
        return parsed;
}
//#endregion
export { loadEnv };

=== Cache file ===
import { existsSync, readFileSync } from "node:fs";
import { parseEnv } from "node:util";
import { expand } from "dotenv-expand";
//#region src/core/utils/env.ts
/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
function loadEnv(mode, browser) {
        const envFiles = [
                `.env`,
                `.env.local`,
                `.env.${mode}`,
                `.env.${mode}.local`,
                `.env.${browser}`,
                `.env.${browser}.local`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`
        ];
        const parsed = Object.fromEntries(envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
                if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
                try {
                        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8"));
                        return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
                } catch {
                        return [];
                }
        }));
        // Set the parsed and expanded values on process.env, respecting any existing
        // environment variables that were already set.
        expand({ parsed });
        return parsed;
}
//#endregion
export { loadEnv };

Let me re-check the expand function:\n\n```js\n// short-circuit scenario: process.env was already set prior to the file value\nif (processEnv[key] && processEnv[key] !== value) {\n  value = processEnv[key]\n}\n```\n\nThis keeps the existing `process.env` value if it's already set and differs from the file value. But if the short-circuit above triggered, `options.parsed[key]` was set to `processEnv[key]`, so it won't actually change anything.\n\nSo the behavior is:\n- If `process.env` already has a key, keep that value\n- If `process.env` doesn't have a key, set it from the parsed+expanded .env file\n\nThis is the correct behavior and matches what `import 'dotenv/config'` would do (dotenv by default doesn't override existing env vars).\n\nThe fix looks complete. This meant that environment variables defined in `.env` files were not available to the application via `process.env`.\n\nThe fix was to remove the copy and let `expand` directly set values on the real `process.env`. === Source ===
import { readFileSync, existsSync } from 'node:fs';
import { parseEnv } from 'node:util';
import { expand } from 'dotenv-expand';
import type { TargetBrowser } from '../../types';

/** Load environment files based on the current mode and browser. */
export function loadEnv(mode: string, browser: TargetBrowser) {
  const envFiles = [
    // List is ordered with general files first, specific ones last, so the more
    // specific files override the more general ones in the loop below.
    `.env`,
    `.env.local`,
    `.env.${mode}`,
    `.env.${mode}.local`,
    `.env.${browser}`,
    `.env.${browser}.local`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
    `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`,
  ];

  const parsed = Object.fromEntries<string>(
    envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
      if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];

      try {
        const content = readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(content);
        return Object.entries(parsedEnv) as [string, string][];
      } catch {
        return [];
      }
    }),
  );

  // Set the parsed and expanded values on process.env, respecting any existing
  // environment variables that were already set.
  expand({ parsed });

  return parsed;
}

=== Dist ===

function loadEnv(mode, browser) {
        const envFiles = [
                `.env`,
                `.env.local`,
                `.env.${mode}`,
                `.env.${mode}.local`,
                `.env.${browser}`,
                `.env.${browser}.local`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}`,
                `.env.${mode}.${browser}.local`
        ];
        const parsed = Object.fromEntries(envFiles.flatMap((filePath) => {
                if (!existsSync(filePath)) return [];
                try {
                        const parsedEnv = parseEnv(readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8"));
                        return Object.entries(parsedEnv);
                } catch {
                        return [];
                }
        }));
        // Set the parsed and expanded values on process.env, respecting any existing
        // environment variables that were already set.
        expand({ parsed });
        return parsed;
}

export { loadEnv };
